## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration, which in oscillator mechanics is typically a restoring-force term derived from a potential energy U(x) (dv_dt = -dU/dx) plus possible explicit time-dependent forcing or time-varying stiffness. With only x and t available (no v), common structures include linear and nonlinear restoring forces in x and externally forced/parametrically excited terms in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear (Hookean) oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x (small-amplitude harmonic motion)
- Shifted equilibrium spring: dv_dt = -c0 * (x - c1) (equilibrium displaced from zero)
- Duffing (hardening/softening) restoring force: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 (c1>0 hardening, c1<0 softening)
- Higher-order polynomial restoring force: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 (strong nonlinearity at large amplitude)
- Bistable (double-well) Duffing form: dv_dt = c0 * x - c1 * x**3 (two stable equilibria when c0>0, c1>0)
- Pendulum restoring torque (angle ~ x): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(x) (bounded restoring force; large-angle pendulum)
- Softening bounded restoring: dv_dt = -c0 * tanh(c1 * x) (restoring saturates at large |x|)
- Piecewise-linear spring (stiffness change): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * Abs(x) * x (effective stiffness increases with |x|)
- Periodic external forcing (additive): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * cos(c2 * t) (driven oscillator)
- Multi-harmonic forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * cos(c2 * t) + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (non-sinusoidal drive decomposition)
- State-dependent forcing amplitude: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * x * cos(c2 * t) (drive couples to displacement)
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (Mathieu-type structure)
- Parametric + cubic nonlinearity: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * x**3 (forced Duffing/Mathieu hybrid)
- Anharmonic potential with cosine term: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) (periodic potential / pendulum-lattice-like restoring)
- Time-modulated equilibrium position: dv_dt = -c0 * (x - c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (moving trap / shaking support)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative oscillator signature: dv_dt depends primarily on x (not t); suggests dv_dt ≈ -dU/dx for some U(x).
- Odd symmetry in x (dv_dt(-x,t) = -dv_dt(x,t)) indicates a symmetric potential about x=0; expect only odd powers of x or sin-like terms.
- Hardening vs softening nonlinearity: adding -c * x**3 changes frequency with amplitude (stiffer with amplitude if coefficient is negative in the equation of motion for x'' + ...).
- Bistability/double-well behavior: dv_dt ≈ c0*x - c1*x**3 implies three equilibria (0 unstable, ±sqrt(c0/c1) stable) and possible switching dynamics under forcing.
- Bounded restoring force: sin(x) or tanh(c*x) structures limit acceleration magnitude at large |x|, typical of pendulum-like or saturation mechanisms.
- Additive periodic terms in t (cos/sin) indicate an external drive; expect resonances when the drive frequency matches the natural frequency.
- Multiplicative cos(c*t)*x terms indicate parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness); expect instability tongues (Mathieu-like resonance regions).
- Presence of multiple harmonics in t suggests non-sinusoidal excitation or nonlinear transduction producing harmonics of the driving frequency.
- Nonzero equilibrium offset terms (x - c) or (x - c*cos(c*t)) indicate shifted/rest moving equilibrium positions (preload, bias, or moving support).

\[
f(x,t)=0.799842060559254\sin t\;-\;1.99164100804766\,x(0.0248350833882069\,t+1)\;-\;1.99164100804766\,x^3\;-\;1.99164100804766\,x.
\]
Combine the linear-in-\(x\) parts:
\[
-1.99164100804766\,x(0.0248350833882069\,t+1)-1.99164100804766\,x
= (-1.99164100804766\cdot 0.0248350833882069)\,t x\;-\;3.98328201609532\,x.
\]
So GT is exactly
\[
f(x,t)=A\,x^3 + B\,t x + C\,x + D\,\sin t
\]
with
- \(A=-1.99164100804766\)
- \(B=-1.99164100804766\cdot 0.0248350833882069\) (some fixed negative number)
- \(C=-3.98328201609532\)
- \(D=0.799842060559254\)

No other functional forms (no logs/exp/max/abs, no extra constants, no \(x^2\), etc.). Any candidate must be reducible to exactly “\(x^3\) + \(t x\) + \(x\) + sinusoid in \(t\)” with the sinusoid being \(\sin t\) up to a phase shift (since \(\cos(t+\phi)=\sin t\) for \(\phi=\pi/2\), etc.).

### Candidate-by-candidate analysis

I’ll check whether each can be parameter-set to: (i) only \(x^3\), \(t x\), \(x\), and one pure trig term in \(t\); (ii) match coefficients; (iii) avoid extra non-removable terms.

1. **\(c0\,t x + c1\,x^3 + c2\cos(c3+t)+c4 x + c5\max(0,c6+x)+c7\cos(c8 t+c9)+x\)**  
   Has a **Max** term depending on \(x\); cannot equal a polynomial for negative \(x\) unless its coefficient is zero: set \(c5=0\). Also has two trig terms; set one to zero: \(c7=0\). Then it can match GT with \(\cos(c3+t)\) phase-shifted to \(\sin t\), and linear \(x\) via \(c4 x + x\). **Potentially matchable**.

2. **\(c0 x + c1 t x + c2 x + c3 x^3 + c4\cos t + c5 x + c6\cos(c7+t)+c8 x\)**  
   Two trig terms; set one amplitude 0 (e.g., \(c6=0\)). Then choose \(c4\cos t\) to represent \(D\sin t\) via phase shift is not possible because it is fixed \(\cos t\) (no phase). But \(\cos t\) cannot equal \(\sin t\) for all \(t\). So unless GT trig were also cosine (it isn’t). Therefore **no match**.

3. Includes \(\log(c4 t+1)\) and constant \(c9\). Log term removable by \(c3=0\); constant removable by \(c9=0\). Then trig terms: \(c2\cos t\) (no phase) plus \(c6\cos(c7+t)\) (phase). Set \(c2=0\) and use \(c6\cos(c7+t)\) to match \(\sin t\). Linear and cubic terms available. **Potentially matchable**.

4. Has extra \(\cos(c8\exp(c9 t))\) which is not a pure sinusoid in \(t\); must set \(c7=0\). Then it reduces to \(t x, x^3, x,\) and two phaseable cos terms; set one cosine amplitude 0. **Potentially matchable**.

5. Has \(c6 x^{c7}\exp(c8 t)\). To avoid non-polynomial/time-coupled exponential, must set \(c6=0\). Then it’s \(t x\) (two coefficients \(c0\) and \(c5\) combine), \(x^3\), one phaseable cosine, and \(x\). **Potentially matchable**.

6. Has \(c5 t (c6+x)^{c7}\) which is not of form \(t x\) unless very special; but even if \(c7=1\), it gives \(c5 t(c6+x)=c5 c6 t + c5 t x\) introducing a pure \(t\) term unless \(c6=0\). Could set \(c5=0\) to remove it. Then it’s \(t x, x^3,\) cosine, \(x\). **Potentially matchable**.

7. Has \(\log(c5 x+1)\) depending on \(x\); must set \(c4=0\). Then only one cosine term (phaseable), \(t x\), \(x^3\), \(x\). **Potentially matchable**.

8. Two \(x^3\) terms (fine), two phaseable cos terms (set one amplitude 0), linear \(x\) terms, and \(t x\). **Potentially matchable**.

9. Has \(\exp(c7 x^2)\) which cannot be polynomial unless \(c6=0\). Then it’s \(x, t x, x^3,\) and one phaseable cosine. **Potentially matchable**.

10. Has \(c2 x^{c3}\). To match GT (which has only \(x^3\) besides linear), set \(c2=0\) (or set \(c3=3\) and merge into cubic, but then you’d have two independent cubic coefficients anyway—still okay). Also has two cos terms; set one amplitude 0. Linear has \(c6 x + x\). **Potentially matchable**.

11. Has \(\cos(c7\exp(c8 x^2))\) depending on \(x\); must set \(c6=0\). Then it’s \(t x\) (two coefficients), \(x^3\), one phaseable cosine, \(x\). **Potentially matchable**.

12. Two phaseable cos terms; set one amplitude 0. Has \(+x\) and \(c4 x\) and \(t x\), \(x^3\). **Potentially matchable**.

13. Single phaseable cosine, \(t x\), \(x^3\), \(c4 x + x\). **Potentially matchable**.

19. Has \(c2 x^{c3}\); set \(c2=0\) (or fold into cubic with \(c3=3\)). Has \(\cos t\) (no phase) and \(\cos(c7+t)\) (phase); set \(c4=0\) and use phaseable one. **Potentially matchable**.

### Construct an explicit match (suffices to prove “match found”)

Use candidate **13**:
\[
c0\,t x + c1\,x^3 + c2\cos(c3+t) + c4 x + x.
\]
Set parameters:
- \(c1 = -1.99164100804766\) (match cubic)
- \(c0 = -1.99164100804766\cdot 0.0248350833882069\) (match \(t x\))
- Choose cosine to become \(D\sin t\): use identity \(\cos(t-\pi/2)=\sin t\).  
  Set \(c3=-\pi/2\), \(c2=0.799842060559254\).
- Linear \(x\): need \(c4 x + x = C x\) so \(c4 = C-1 = -3.98328201609532 - 1 = -4.98328201609532\).

Then candidate 13 becomes exactly the GT for all real \(x,t\).

Therefore at least one candidate can be made mathematically equivalent to GT.
